Memorial Service for Martyrs and Compatriots Who Died in the Anti-Japanese War

Today's Meeting at the City Chamber of Commerce

Central Party Headquarters and National Government Send Representatives

Army Commander Cai Tingkai and Others Personally Attend to Offer Sacrifices, Security is Tight, Nearby Traffic Temporarily Cut Off

City Lowers Flags to Half-Mast, Suspends Banquets and Entertainment

The Shanghai All-Circles Memorial Meeting for the Fallen Soldiers and Deceased Compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War was held at 10:00 AM today at the Chamber of Commerce near Tianhou Palace Bridge. The Central National Government and other organizations sent personnel to offer sacrifices. Army Commander Cai, Division Commander Qu, and Brigade Commander Weng all personally attended. All arrangements for the meeting venue have been completed, and temporary security is tight. The details are as follows:

Arrangements Completed. At the entrance of the meeting venue, a white archway was erected, with the Party and National flags and a plaque hanging on it. In the center was "Righteous Spirit Will Endure Forever," on the east side was "Heroic Souls Still Exist," on the west side was "Spirit Never Dies," and below was "Shanghai All-Circles Memorial Meeting for the Fallen Soldiers and Deceased Compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War." On both sides of the entrance, mourning couplets were hung. The entrance of the auditorium was also decorated with彩帶 (彩帶 are decorative ribbons). Mourning couplets were hung on both sides, and various slogans were eye-catching, such as "The Anti-Japanese Responsibilities Not Fulfilled by the Fallen Soldiers Are All On Us, the Survivors," "The Songhu Anti-Japanese War Was the Prelude to the Rejuvenation of the Chinese Nation," "We Must Continue the Spirit of the Fallen Soldiers," etc. The arrangement of the altar was very solemn and grand. On the stage was a seven-tiered stupa made of pine and cypress, with the spirit tablets of the martyrs in the center, surrounded by portraits of the martyrs. All the equipment was arranged last night. The National Products Department Store, Watson's Soda Company, and Yicheng Company have prepared to sacrifice everything to offer soda, cigarettes, and beer.

Meeting Order (1) Gathering (Chinese Police Bell Rings), (2) Commander Leads the Chief and Assistant Sacrificers to Take Their Seats, (3) Representatives of Party, Government, and Military Organizations Take Their Seats, (4) Guest Observers Take Their Seats, (5) Everyone Stands at Attention, (6) Play Mournful Music (Garrison Headquarters Band), (7) Sing the Party Song, (8) Give the Highest Salute to the Party and National Flags and the Portrait of Sun Yat-sen (Bow), (9) Give the Highest Salute to the Fallen Soldiers and Deceased Compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War (Three Bows), (10) Observe Three Minutes of Silence to Mourn the Fallen Soldiers and Deceased Compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War (Bell Rings), (11) Chief Sacrificer Delivers a Eulogy, (12) Chief Sacrificer Presents a Wreath, (13) Read the Memorial Text, (14) Party, Government, and Military Representatives Offer Sacrifices, (1) Three Bows, (2) Read the Memorial Text, (15) Play Mournful Music (Datong Music Society), (16) Shout Slogans, (17) Play Mournful Music (Public Security Bureau Band), (18) Ceremony Concludes.

Duties and Assignments Chief Sacrificer: Xiaolai. Assistant Sacrificers: All Preparatory Committee Members. General Commander: Li Yongxiang. Deputy Commander: Zhang Yichen. Chief Inspector: Wang Gang. Deputy Inspector: Liu Zhongying. Health Director: Wang Peiyuan. Chief Receptionist: Zheng Chengqing. Deputy Receptionist: Chen Kecheng. Security Director: Zhang Taiji. Deputy Director: Huang Ming. Reader of the Memorial Text: Cao Zhigong. Master of Ceremonies: Huang Zaoxiong. The Chinese Boy Scouts Council sends 200 Boy Scouts from the Chamber of Commerce, postal workers, Moor Hall, and silk workers to maintain order at the meeting. The Municipal Public Security Bureau's police brigade sends 100 armed police officers, 10 inspectors from the Supervisory Office, 10 detectives from the Detective Team, 30 members from the Shanghai North Security Corps, and all members of the Chamber of Commerce Security Corps to provide protection.

Tight Security The Public Concession's Municipal Council Police Department has dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western armed detectives to guard near the meeting venue at North Suzhou Road, Henan Road, and Shanxi Road to prevent any incidents. All vehicles of guests are not allowed to enter the venue, and traffic to and from the Chamber of Commerce is temporarily cut off, only allowing cars attending the meeting to pass. The Chamber of Commerce, in order to prevent incidents, has specially distributed commemorative badges in advance. Guests enter the meeting with badges, and those without badges are refused entry.

Citywide Mourning The Municipal Government, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Citizens' Federation, the General Federation of Commerce of All Roads, and the General Labor Union have all notified their subordinates to lower flags to half-mast today, wear black紗 (紗 is a type of gauze/fabric) armbands, and suspend all entertainment banquets to mourn the loyal souls. The Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Control Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, Garrison Commander Dai Ji, 19th Route Army Commander Cai Tingkai, 78th Division Commander Qu Shounian, 156th Brigade Commander Weng Zhaoyuan, the 5th Army's 88th Division, the 87th Division, and others all participated in the memorial service.

Memorial Text The memorial meeting for the fallen soldiers of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War was held in Suzhou on May 28th. All circles in Shanghai believe that Songhu is the place where the generals and soldiers died for their country, and there were also many civilian casualties. A grand commemoration must be held. Therefore, it is scheduled to hold another memorial meeting in Shanghai on the 12th of this month. We respectfully offer incense, flowers, fresh fruits, and sacrifices to the fallen generals and soldiers and the deceased compatriots, saying: Alas, the powerful neighbor started the war, affecting the Shanghai region. The generals and soldiers defended the country with unwavering loyalty. The lone army defended bitterly for nearly forty days. The bravery in battle and the frequency of casualties are shining brightly in the rivers and mountains, and the righteousness moves ghosts and gods. The enemy soldiers raged, more than the violent Qin. Where the swords and arrows pointed, it spread to the civilians. Sand worms and cranes all shared this destruction. More than three months have passed, and the blood stains are still fresh. The affairs of the time, life is like a grain of dust. Where great righteousness lies, bones are shattered. The spirit of the Chinese nation has been slightly extended. The enemy's fear has been suppressed, and a temporary peace has been achieved. The army is withdrawn and the armor is stored. We, the survivors, are filled with mixed feelings. We offer raw sacrifices and recommend兕觥 (兕觥 a bronze wine vessel), not to seek blessings, but to comfort the elite spirits. Alas, in the white mountains and black waters, the enemy cavalry is rampant. Killing fills the fields, bones are broken, and hearts are shocked. Whose millet porridge is offered to the bones in the wilderness? Comparing this to that, we are all ordinary people. Heaven, how cruel, hot tears fill our eyes. Alas, in the coming great calamity, the nation and the society will collapse. The people are still in a drunken stupor. The officials who built the节 (節 segment/knot/festival) are still engaged in internal strife. The loyal souls and their blood cannot comfort the nine springs. May we, the people, work hard for the future. On this day next year, we will offer sacrifices again. Accept the offering.

Zhang Zhizhong's Eulogy Army Commander Zhang Zhizhong of the 5th Army of the National Revolutionary Army, leading all the officers and soldiers, says in his eulogy: On June 12th, the 21st year of the Republic of China, all circles in Shanghai held a memorial meeting for the fallen soldiers and deceased compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War. We respectfully offer this eulogy: The Japanese pirates are stupid and foolish, the moths of justice, plotting to seize our Liaoning and coveting our Shanghai. Relying on our soldiers and civilians, united as one, we cooperated in resisting and did not avoid sacrifice. Blood dyed Jiangwan, corpses filled the Huangpu River. Our spirit penetrates the sun and moon, our voice shakes the universe. Fragrant flowers and fine wine, we cry and mourn for the fallen. Our martyrs are the light of the nation.

Dai Ji's Memorial Text Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji offers a memorial text, saying: On June 12th, the 21st year of the Republic of China, Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji respectfully offers clear wine and fresh flowers to the spirits of the fallen soldiers and deceased compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War, saying: The夷 (夷 ancient barbarian) people have been our enemies for generations, taking advantage of our荒祲 (荒祲 famine), their poisonous claws flow rampantly. On September 18th, they attacked Shenyang, changing the color of our territory, and our golden 瓯 (瓯 earthenware cup) was not completed. After a year of aggression and plunder, the world is worried. On January 28th, Zhabei was trampled upon, our territory and our land, witnessed by the world. If there is no battle, the nation will die. Alas, our officers and soldiers, pierced chests and broken heads, blood and flesh, and sharp weapons, incomparable sincerity. The strong changed their vision, and the alleys began to sing. The tragic compatriots were murdered, their houses were burned, and their lives were lost. The widows, orphans, and children were displaced and could not be gathered. The old and weak filled the gullies, and the young and strong shared their hatred. Neighborhood assistance in the war, carrying millet and helping with oars, the grey heads rose like clouds, and the Han banners rose like the wind. The poor and the snow, and the spears and halberds of the sea, the united will formed a city, and the righteous and courageous banners marched. It was not only military power, but also the reliance on the people's wisdom. Iron or blood, ten thousand years and a thousand autumns. Alas, alas, accept the offering.

Meeting Declaration The meeting printed a declaration yesterday, which will be distributed to the representatives attending the meeting today. The text reads: Today we are holding this memorial meeting for the fallen soldiers and deceased compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War. We truly have unspeakable grief and pain. "Our magnificent Chinese nation is not respected by the great powers, and our dignified people are treated lightly by foreign races." This has been the case for a long time. In recent times, the imperialists have intensified their efforts, especially Japanese hegemony, destroying the integrity of our territory and killing our innocent compatriots. One after another, events like the May 30th Incident, disregarding humanity and justice, relying on the precision of their cannons, and carrying out the atrocities of beasts. Wherever their iron hooves reached, the sky became dark. Now, the flames of the September 18th Incident have not yet been extinguished, and the disaster of January 28th has come again. It is hair-raising to speak of. Alas, our Chinese nation has suffered a hundred years of double oppression. The nation's vitality has reached its extreme point. Although it is said that the National Revolution has been successful, and that saving the country through the Party has achieved its goal, we have found that internal affairs are not easily sorted out, and revolutionary construction cannot be discussed. Moreover, there are shameless warlords, indulging in wine and sex, putting the duty of resisting foreign enemies and defending the country out of their minds. There is no way to cover up their shame of non-resistance. They borrow the beautiful name of "bearing humiliation and bearing responsibility" or "whole resistance" to unload their guilt. Wood rots and then worms are born. If our own spirit is like this, how can we expect Japan, which has been eyeing us for a long time, to restrain its ambition? The people have the heart to save the country, but lack the means to die for it. Although they loudly call for and advocate resistance against Japan, the environment is so restrictive that they can only be angry and speechless. Therefore, the government authorities have been making all kinds of concessions, hoping to gain the final pity of the imperialists who are waiting to kill. Anti-Japanese patriotic groups have been closed down, and the movement to boycott enemy goods has been virtually canceled. But Japan, whose arrow is on the string and cannot be held back, is still not satisfied. After claiming to be satisfied, they immediately follow up with bombings by airplanes and cannons. It goes without saying that such barbaric acts lack humanity and justice, and simply despise the national integrity of our Republic of China. Their attitude is as insulting as a violent husband towards a weak wife, making her laugh and cry, according to their whims. Fortunately, our 19th Route Army did not disgrace the duty of soldiers, and was not afraid of the Japanese bandits. They were determined to sacrifice themselves and resist to the end, even if the last bullet was fired. With an iron spirit, they stood firm on the mountain of corpses and in the sea of blood, never changing their original intention. As soon as the righteous banner was raised, the people rejoiced. The Fifth Army also loved the country and did not dare to lag behind, rising up to fight together and share the difficulties. The officers and soldiers fought desperately on the front lines, and the people assisted in the rear, and finally achieved the effect of repelling the enemy. After holding out for thirty-four days, the Japanese imperialists, even with their superior cannons and soldiers, not only failed to gain the slightest advantage, but also suffered heavy casualties and losses. And our brave soldiers, who sacrificed for the nation, for the country, for justice, and for righteousness, are countless. At this time, the violent Japanese, unable to win in military terms, were furious and carried out a great massacre, killing our good compatriots and burning our homes. Bones and flesh were scattered everywhere, and ruins were everywhere. The pain was so great that it could not be added to. Thinking of our dead compatriots, although they are not as great in merit as the fallen soldiers, the cruelty of the imperialists is thus more clearly revealed, making the survivors more determined to rise up and resist Japan, and this also has its own meaning. Now the ceasefire agreement has been signed on the bed, and the invading Japanese soldiers have said that they will withdraw and return to their country.

The talk of a round table conference is now being lobbied for by the Japanese side. Although the Japanese government has its own overall plan and the Japanese people have their own dreams, we remember the January 28th Resistance, the intense and tragic morale, the hot-blooded surge of the people, and the result is only remaining corpses and bones exposed on the battlefield, broken buildings and ruins piled up in Songhu, economic devastation, millions of unemployed, and a broken society that cannot be reversed. How can those who have not died not be in deep pain and sorrow multiplied? And our fallen soldiers and deceased compatriots, if they knew in the afterlife, would surely have their hair standing on end and their eyes cracking, and they would cry bitterly. Our empty words of remembrance are of no help. We must quickly awaken ourselves, shoulder the unfinished heavy responsibility of the dead, and urge the government to unite as one, not to be subdued by force, not to be tempted by profit, and continue to resist Japan to the death. Only in this way can we live up to the meaning of today's memorial service, and stand before the spirits of the great fallen soldiers and deceased compatriots without shame. In addition to grief, the conference cannot express all of its intentions, and it humbly recounts them, and hereby informs our compatriots from all walks of life. (New Voice Society)

Propaganda Outline (1) The January 28th Shanghai Incident and the September 18th Northeast Incident are both consistent traditional policies of Japanese imperialism's invasion of China. (2) The withdrawal of Japanese soldiers back to their country is a diplomatic strategy. The Japanese had already indicated at the League of Nations that "the Shanghai Incident can be conceded, but the Northeast Incident should not be interfered with by a third party." This shows that it is not a sincere expression of peace. The withdrawal of troops from Shanghai is only to ease the international atmosphere and to facilitate the thorough success of the Northeast invasion. (3) The responsibility for the Shanghai Incident should be borne by Japan. The Chinese side has always maintained calm, even canceling anti-Japanese groups, in order to seek peace. Unexpectedly, the Japanese attacked that night after claiming to be satisfied, causing the destruction of Shanghai, where world commerce gathers. How can the Japanese be allowed to shirk their responsibility? (4) The Japanese soldiers in Shanghai have not yet been completely withdrawn, and the voice of the free city is becoming more and more audible. Although this is a dream of the Japanese, Japan, which is good at seduction, will surely do its best to incite various countries. The future is truly worrying. This shows that Japan's ceasefire is not sincere. We should expose their ambitions and warn our people to pay attention and prevent them at all times. (5) The fact that Shanghai did not become the Northeast this time is entirely the price paid by the 19th Route Army's heavy sacrifices. From this, we know more about the absurdity of the non-resistance policy. The first way out for the Chinese people from now on is to seek it through unity and continued resistance. (6) From the suffering of the deceased compatriots, we have a deeper understanding of the ferocity and cruelty of Japanese imperialism. We should strive to strengthen the country and fight them to the death in order to save the nation from its critical plight. (7) In mourning the fallen soldiers, we should urge the government to implement resistance and revolutionary diplomacy to fulfill the anti-Japanese aspirations of the dead, and to commend and comfort their merits and their surviving families in order to inspire the loyalty and bravery of the surviving soldiers. (8) The death of the deceased compatriots is due to the poverty and weakness of the country. We should also urge the government and all circles to find ways to appease their surviving families in order to comfort the dead and maintain the people's hearts. (9) After the January 28th Incident, the war zones have all become desolate ruins. The affected areas of Nanshi and the concessions have also suffered considerable losses. We should urge the government and all circles to find ways to remedy the situation and reverse the calamity in one out of ten thousand cases. (10) As for implementing economic severance, promoting domestic goods, and boycotting Japanese goods, this is especially an urgent task. Our people should practice what they preach and not neglect it. (11) When we mourn the fallen soldiers and deceased compatriots, it is not enough to simply observe three minutes of silence for the dead, send a few wreaths, and hang a few mourning couplets. We should never forget their death, the reason for their death, and continue their legacy and their unfinished work. Printed by the Shanghai All-Circles Memorial Meeting for the Fallen Soldiers and Deceased Compatriots of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War, June 12th.

Special Martial Law Today

Due to No Meeting Allowed at Public Sports Field

Iron Gates at the Border Between Chinese and Concessions Temporarily Closed

The Shanghai People's Association Against the Ceasefire Agreement and Supporting the Northeast Volunteer Army originally scheduled to convene a memorial meeting for Gu Zhenghong and the martyrs who died in the anti-Japanese war on "May 30th." However, due to special martial law imposed by the Chinese and Concession authorities and traffic obstruction, the meeting was postponed to the 5th. Later, in order to expand the scope, it was changed again to 10:00 AM today at the West Gate Public Sports Field to hold a memorial meeting for the martyrs who died in the anti-Japanese war in the Northeast and Songhu. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, on the grounds that the meeting had not been approved and that it was during a period of martial law, how could it hold a meeting without authorization, ordered its subordinates to ban it. It also declared special martial law today. The police brigades, sections, and substations in all districts were all armed and deployed. Double posts were stationed at all important roads, and patrols were stepped up. The Public Concession and French Concession police departments were also ordered to be on high alert. The iron gates at the border between the Chinese and concessions were all closed, leaving only one or two small doors to allow vehicles to pass. Chinese and Western detectives were also increased.

Checking pedestrians at the border, and the People's Association Against the Ceasefire Agreement and Supporting the Northeast Volunteer Army erected a platform on the stage at the West Gate Public Sports Field yesterday morning in preparation for today's meeting. After receiving the report, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, on the grounds that the meeting was being held during martial law, ordered the police to

Remove the platform, and the doors and windows on all four sides of the public sports field were closed, prohibiting the meeting from being held.

Japan

Third Fleet Leaves Shanghai

Nomura, Shiozawa, Uematsu, etc.

Returned Home Yesterday on the Izumo Battleship

The Second Fleet of the Japanese Navy, which was transferred to Shanghai on February 3rd, has been there for more than four months. It was not until yesterday that it finally set sail and returned home. Nomura, Shiozawa, Uematsu, Shimada, etc., also boarded the

Izumo battleship to return home. The details are as follows:

Flagship Sets Sail After arriving in Shanghai on February 3rd, the flagship Izumo of the Japanese Navy's Third Fleet was stationed in front of the Japanese Consulate, commonly known as the Mitsubishi Wharf. An electric網 (網 net/web) was set up around the hull of the ship. At 5:00 AM yesterday, it received Nomura's order to move from in front of the Mitsubishi Wharf to moor in front of the Osaka Wharf in Yangshupu. The military equipment and supplies belonging to the Third Fleet, which were stored in various warehouses in Yangshupu, were then moved onto the ship. The light cruiser Tokiwa was also re-moored there. At 12:40 PM, it began to leave Shanghai.

Nomura Boards Ship Third Fleet Commander Vice Admiral Nomura, accompanied by the newly appointed Director of the Naval Education Bureau, Rear Admiral Shiozawa, and the outgoing Commander of the Marines, Uematsu, as well as Third Fleet Staff Officer Rear Admiral Shimada, etc., arrived at the wharf by car at about 12:00 PM. The Marines then dispatched a team of soldiers led by Major Ota to set up guard posts in the wharf area, not allowing pedestrians to stop and watch.

Japanese Nationals See Off Those who went to the wharf to see off included the newly appointed Commander of the Japanese Navy's Shanghai Special Marine Corps, Rear Admiral Sugi 板 (杉板 cedar plank), Samejima, Kitaoka, two staff officers, the leader of the Chamber of Commerce, Miri, a representative of the textile industry, Funatsu, and various representatives of Japanese nationals, totaling more than 200 people. There were farewell flags written on the wharf, and a team of elementary school students also went to the wharf to see them off. At 12:40 PM, the Izumo finally carried the military officers away from Shanghai and returned home.

Farewell Remarks Nomura delivered farewell remarks to those seeing him off on the Izumo, saying that he was injured during the 天長節 (Emperor's Birthday celebration) and thought he would secretly die in the hospital. Now he is fortunate to have fully recovered, and today he is leaving Shanghai and returning home. He hopes that the Shanghai people will work harder to achieve peace in East Asia, and so on.

Existing Japanese Warships The Japanese warships on the Yangtze River during the war and the Japanese warships in Shanghai were almost united as one. At most, there were 65 ships. The ships in Shanghai are now gradually withdrawing. There are still 15 teams of four torpedoes, which can also set sail tomorrow. From today onwards, the Japanese warships in Shanghai will still belong to the First Foreign Dispatch Team of the Yangtze River, but in reality, there are six more ships than before January 28th.

Japanese Marines

Withdraw Completely in the Shortest Possible Time

Japanese Committee Member Okazaki Formally Replied Yesterday

Hua Dong News Agency said that regarding the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops, Mr. Yu Hongjun, a member of our side of the Joint Committee, has made serious representations to Japanese Committee Member Katsuo Okazaki on several occasions. The Japanese side stated that the commander of the Special Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai was in the process of transition between the old and the new, and a formal reply could only be given to our side after the handover procedures were completed on the 11th. At 11:50 AM yesterday, Japanese Committee Member Okazaki formally visited Secretary-General Yu at the Municipal Government as agreed to reply to this question. According to the Japanese Committee, the procedures for the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops have been negotiated with Colonel Sugiita, the new commander of the Japanese Marines, and it has been decided to withdraw completely within a few days. However, because the number of Japanese troops currently stationed in Shanghai is greater than before the war, the original garrison locations in the concession are not enough to accommodate them. In the short term, it is still necessary to negotiate garrison locations with the concession authorities. Therefore, the withdrawal date has not yet been determined. However, the Japanese side sincerely hopes that this difficulty can be resolved as soon as possible in the shortest possible time, so that the withdrawal procedures will not be delayed. On the one hand, it also deeply hopes that our country's authorities will understand. After listening to Yu's remarks, he said that although what the Japanese Committee said was for other reasons, according to the spirit of the agreement, those Japanese troops could no longer remain stationed. Moreover, rumors have been rampant in recent days, causing uneasiness among Chinese and foreign residents. Therefore, he still firmly demanded that the Japanese side withdraw immediately and should quickly set a withdrawal date. The Japanese Committee immediately expressed acceptance. The talks lasted for 30 minutes before he left.

Xinsheng News Agency said that Secretary Lang of the Joint Committee told the reporter of the Xinsheng News Agency in a telephone call the other day that the issue of the complete withdrawal of the Japanese Navy will have new

Developments on the 13th (Monday). At the same time, the Public Concession will begin to lift martial law. At that time, the phone was buzzing, and it was mistaken for a formal reply on the 13th. I will correct it in this order.

Japanese Commander Visits Mayor Wu Colonel Sugiita, commander of the Japanese Navy's Shanghai Special Marine Corps, accompanied by Bai Jinglian, Deputy Consul of the Japanese Consulate, and Kamata Masakazu, Adjutant of the Marine Corps Staff, formally visited Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Public Security Director Wen Yingxing at the Municipal Government at 11:00 AM yesterday, since the handover procedures have been completed. Wu and Wen received them, and Mr. Ban Rugeng, a member of our Municipal Government, served as the interpreter, and Shirai Yasushi served as the interpreter for the Japanese side.

The two sides had a茗談 (茗談 literally "tea talk," meaning informal conversation) for about half an hour before leaving.

Japanese Navy's Actions in West Shanghai According to Liu Yunfang, the director of the second section of the sixth district, the Municipal Public Security Bureau reported yesterday that at about 8:00 AM the day before yesterday, according to Liu Gancheng, the police chief of the Hongqiao police station, a truck carrying about 20 Japanese soldiers drove out of the 同文書院 (Tongwen College) and left. At 9:20, a military vehicle carrying more than 10 Japanese soldiers and military supplies came to the 同文書院 (Tongwen College). It was not until 9:30 that they left. At 11:00 and 12:00, there were two military vehicles, carrying about 30 Japanese soldiers in total, to the hospital. Most of the above-mentioned Japanese soldiers were stationed in the Chinese Ministry. Every night, three or five Marines from the Marine Corps stationed in the ministry would pass through Hongqiao Road, Triumphal Road, and Columbia Road, patrolling back and forth. Also, the old students of the Chinese Ministry, which was formerly located in the Chinese Ministry, have now been merged and attend classes with Japanese students as usual, without any significant actions.

Song Ziwen's Speech

No Debts Incurred Since April

Revenue and Expenditure Perfectly Balanced

My Energy and Strength Exhausted

Difficult to Shoulder the Heavy Responsibility of Finance Again

After submitting his resignation, Minister of Finance Song Ziwen remained silent for almost a week. Yesterday, he suddenly released a statement worthy of attention. We hereby record it as follows:

Over the past year, I have been unfortunately beset by both public and private affairs. Therefore, at the end of the year, I resigned and went to Hangzhou for recuperation. However, with the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, the powerful neighbor pressing in, and the atmosphere of war escalating, I felt that the overall situation was critical and that every man had a responsibility. Disregarding everything, I rushed to Nanjing day and night to reassume the position of Minister of Finance. At that time, the national treasury was extremely empty, while military salaries and expenses were urgently needed. Amidst internal and external troubles, I devised various plans, hoping to restore public confidence in the government on the one hand, and secure resources for resisting the enemy on the other. At the same time, it was also necessary to consider the stability of the market and finance. Therefore, on the day of my reinstatement, I immediately began to reorganize government bonds, aiming to ensure that the credit of the bonds would not decline and would be further guaranteed, while also reducing the government's monthly debt burden. Fortunately, bondholders at that time were deeply aware of the greater good, and the reorganization plan was successfully completed. Those provinces that had been intercepting national taxes were strictly ordered to remit them to the central government, and military and administrative expenses were actively reduced. The national order was gradually restored to its former state. Although in recent months, first the Japanese army invaded Shanghai with continuous flames of war, and then the truce agreement was on the verge of collapse, the government has always been diligent and self-disciplined, following a policy of austerity and proceeding painfully. Therefore, in the recent month of April, the government did not incur a single debt, and revenue and expenditure were able to be balanced, which is something I am extremely gratified about. During the Japanese invasion of Shanghai, banks and financial institutions in Shanghai were constantly in turmoil. Being located in Shanghai, it was even necessary to lend large sums to the government. I knew that once the market's confidence was lost, the national finance would collapse, and the country would be doomed. Now that the Shanghai incident has come to an end, my energy and strength are exhausted, and I am truly unable to shoulder the heavy responsibility of finance again. From what I have observed, the future financial difficulties may be even greater than they are today, though perhaps not as urgent as in the past few months. This is because the expenditure on military and administrative expenses will likely increase rather than decrease. However, even if administrative expenses increase slightly, it will not be difficult to raise funds. The suppression of the Communist bandits is currently the most pressing problem. If the Communist bandits are not eliminated for a single day, the foundation of the country will not be solid for a single day. The government's only major responsibility is to thoroughly eliminate the Communist bandits in the Yangtze River basin. Now that Chairman Jiang has been entrusted with this responsibility, it can be said that the right person has been chosen. Mr. Jiang is courageous in taking on responsibilities, and we deeply hope that he will persevere and achieve the goal of complete elimination. Since April, the government has made various efforts to economize and has fortunately overcome difficulties, establishing a foundation for balanced income and expenditure. Future construction projects can therefore have a foothold. I am extremely gratified in my heart. However, looking around the country, there are widespread scenes of suffering, with disasters affecting all industries and millions of rural villages being almost completely ravaged by the Communist bandits. In addition, the strong neighbor has invaded, and the wounds have not yet healed. How can we further increase taxes and inflict more suffering on our people? Although in recent weeks, national tax revenues have exceeded my expectations and have not decreased significantly, there is a principle in economics called the law of diminishing returns. Should those in charge of finance not pay attention to this principle during this difficult period? Since tax revenues cannot be increased, the only way is to incur debts. This is like cutting flesh to mend sores, repeating the cycle until there is no more flesh to cut. Is incurring debts any different? If the annual revenue is insufficient, then debts are incurred to make up for it. If there is no way to repay the debts, then new debts are incurred to repay them. Eventually, all the income of the national treasury is used to repay debts, and it is still not enough. I have already tasted the pain in this. In the recent month of April, thanks to various efforts to economize and the great righteousness and sacrifice of national bondholders, this terrifying cycle of the past few years was finally broken. This is a blessing for the country and also a personal fortune. No matter how much the government needs in terms of finance, I feel guilty in my heart and will never follow this evil cycle again. However, the Communist bandits are rampant and cannot be eliminated without a large army. With a large army gathered, military expenses must increase. I am ashamed of my lack of talent and have no way to respond. It is just like a difficult problem in physics: when an irresistible force advances, it suddenly encounters an immovable object. What will be the result? My situation is similar to this. For the sake of the overall situation and from a personal standpoint, I have no choice but to resign. Furthermore, can we not survive without incurring debts? When the world is hungry, vegetable roots can also satisfy hunger. Why must we eat meat porridge? It is good to increase revenue, but if there is no way to increase revenue, the only way is to reduce expenditure. The effect of reducing expenditure has already been seen. Can we not continue to do so and further innovate internally to seek a bright path? The problem of the Communist bandits is not simply a military problem, nor is it simply a political problem. Using military force to suppress the Communist bandits and using politics to pacify the people will ensure that the Communist bandits will not rise again after they are eliminated. Otherwise, they will rise up one after another, and it will be difficult to eradicate their roots. The current economic downturn has reached the world, and those who suffer from it are not only China. The key is to deal with it properly. Looking around Europe and the United States, all are advocating austerity. Countries in the East and West have already done this before us. Diligence and self-discipline are the reasons for our party's success. Because we were able to be diligent, the warlords fled at the sight of the party army, and the people welcomed us with food and drink. That is why we have today. Because we were able to be diligent, even the rampant Japanese eventually lowered their flags and retreated. What we can do today, those who come after us should also be able to do. If we are united and work hard, what do we have to fear from crossing this turbulent sea and achieving prosperity and strength? It depends on the government and the people to do well. My resignation will not affect the political situation. Although I am leaving, I feel at ease. In recent years, I have resigned several times because of the huge expenses and the lack of a magic touch to make money. However, in the end, I was unable to do so because I had not fulfilled my responsibility to the bondholders. Now, it is different. The bonds have been reorganized this time, and those who succeed me should be able to maintain the status quo without difficulty. Although I dare not say that the financial system I have implemented is perfect, the fact that I have been able to achieve a balance between income and expenditure amidst internal and external troubles without incurring a single debt in four months is a foolish idea that may be useful for those who succeed me to learn from. As for the likin tax, which has harmed the country and the people for a hundred years, and all taxes similar to the likin, which I have always hated, they have been fundamentally eradicated under the supervision and active assistance of Chairman Jiang and Mr. Hu. Also, the Central Bank, which I have managed, now has a solid foundation and stands firmly as a pillar of the national finance. Those who succeed me should be able to make good use of it.

Local News Two

Cunningham Denies

Convening of Roundtable Conference

Japanese Newspaper Criticizes the Public Works Department

The Ta Kung Pao reported that a representative of the Ta Kung Pao yesterday afternoon (the 10th) took a copy of a Tokyo telegram received by the Japanese United Press on the 9th to visit the American Consul General Cunningham, asking if it was true that the Japanese Foreign Ministry had received information that the Shanghai consular body would hold a meeting soon to discuss the roundtable conference. Mr. Cunningham replied that he was not aware that the consular body would hold this meeting and had not heard of this news before. However, Mr. Cunningham's words were very different from those of Iguchi, the acting Japanese Consul General in Shanghai, as reported in yesterday's Japanese-language Shanghai Mainichi Shimbun. Iguchi said that various foreign chambers of commerce in Shanghai had requested the consular body to hold a roundtable conference in Shanghai, and the members of the consular body would hold a meeting to discuss this matter, but it was not known whether the consular body would request to convene a roundtable conference. As for the Public Works Department's plan to resolve the issue of road construction beyond the boundaries with the special committee of the Shanghai Municipal Government, yesterday's Japanese newspapers in Shanghai strongly criticized this, saying that the Public Works Department had no right to interfere in this matter and that it should be handled by the consular body or the roundtable conference.

Playing with Shells

Three Seamstresses Tragically Die

Seamstresses Pick Up a Shell on Baoshan Road

Forcefully Hammering, the Shell Suddenly Explodes and Bombs

Three Male and Female Workers Die Tragically

Ye Shaoyu, a Cantonese, is a red gang tailor. He set up a workshop at No. 531 Hong'an Lane, Bazilu (Targets Road), employing seamstresses Chen Guo, Wang Qian, and Liang Shengyu to make Western suits and shirts for various clothing stores. Recently, because the Dragon Boat Festival had just passed, the work was not busy, and the seamstresses had plenty of free time. Yesterday afternoon, Chen and Wang initiated a tour of the war zone to pay their respects to the broken walls and scorched earth of Baoshan Road. Walking near the Commercial Press, they picked up a shell from a pile of rubble and took it home as a souvenir. Around 7:30 p.m., after finishing their dinner, the seamstresses were chatting idly in the front wing room. Chen and Wang took out the shell they had picked up during the day to play with. At that time, in addition to Chen Guo, Wang Qian, and Liang Shengyu, there was also Ye Hongdao, the younger brother of the workshop owner Ye Shaoyu, in the room. After Chen and Wang stroked the shell for a while, they still felt unsatisfied and suddenly began to knock and peel it in order to further study it and examine the contents of the shell. In an instant, everyone in the house heard a loud crash coming from the front wing room, followed by the smell of gunpowder entering their noses. They followed the sound and rushed to the wing room to see what had happened. But the four people, Chen, Wang, Liang, and Ye, were lying horizontally and vertically on the floor. The objects in the room were in a mess, falling to the ground, and wisps of green smoke were still slowly seeping out of the cracks in the door. Soon, the Hongkou Police Station heard the news and immediately ordered the fire brigade to drive to the scene to collect the four people. Western detective Hair Hua and detective Feng Qi arrived at the scene to investigate and found that Chen Guo and Wang Qian had already died under the shell. Although Ye Xi and Liang Shengyu were not dead, they were covered in blood and flesh and were unconscious. They were sent to Tongren Hospital and Guangren Hospital for treatment respectively. At 9:15 p.m. last night, Liang Shengyu died of serious injuries. Chen Guo, the deceased, was 21 years old, and Wang Qian was also 21 years old and was of Cantonese origin. The injured Ye Hongxi had his left foot broken, and the seamstress Liang Shengyu was also injured all over her body, and their lives were in danger. The shell picked up by the seamstresses was about a foot high and looked like a thermos bottle. It was said that when the accident occurred, iron tools were used to hammer and chisel the shell, causing the explosives to be shocked and explode on the ground. The explosive power of this shell was huge. In addition to the four dead and injured, the objects, utensils, walls, and wooden boards in the room were also damaged, either destroyed or penetrated. The deaths of Chen and Wang were extremely tragic. Wang Qian's hands, feet, and limbs were all blown off, and his chest was also sunken into a hole. Chen Guo's head was destroyed and his face was torn, with blood and flesh blurred and unbearable to look at. Both bodies were sent to the coroner's office to await examination by the court. The four unfortunate seamstresses had only lived in this house for a month, as Ye Shaoyu moved into this house in mid-May. Counting on their fingers, it was only a little over thirty days.

Municipal Government

Sends Letter Requesting the Withdrawal of British Troops

The Municipal Government stated that during the Songhu War, British troops stationed in Shanghai were stationed on Bailinan Road and Kaixuan Road. Negotiations had been conducted previously, but they were dismissed as temporary measures and have not been withdrawn. Yesterday, another letter was sent to the British Consul in Shanghai, requesting their speedy withdrawal in order to strengthen friendship. The original letter is as follows: Sir, I am writing to you to inquire about the case of the deployment of your country's troops beyond the boundaries. Previously, this government sent a letter to your Consul General requesting him to forward it to stop this. Later, on February 5, your Consul General replied that it was a temporary measure and that it could be stopped when the situation permitted. Now that the Shanghai Truce Agreement has been signed and the Japanese troops are withdrawing one after another, the situation has calmed down. This government's police force is fully capable of maintaining local security. This government shall be fully responsible for the lives and property of all foreign nationals in this city. It is now found that there are still troops from your country stationed on Qiaodun Road near Columbia Road, Bailinan Road, and the west side of Kaixuan Road. We request your Consul General to forward this to the military authorities of your country to quickly withdraw the troops from the above two locations in order to respect sovereignty and strengthen friendship. We hereby send this letter and hope for your consideration and a reply. Respectfully, to John Brenan, British Consul General in Shanghai.

American

Army to Return to Philippines

July 1st

The Ta Mei Wan Pao reported that the 1st Battalion of the 31st Infantry Regiment of the US Army, which was transferred from the Philippines to Shanghai on February 5 after the outbreak of the Shanghai War and stationed in places such as the New World, has been here for more than four months. Because the situation in Shanghai has eased, it received a telegram from Washington last night ordering it to set sail for the Philippines on July 1. The US Army transport ship Republic will arrive in Shanghai from Tianjin on June 30, and the US troops will board the ship on that day and set sail for Manila the next day. It is said that the US Army's stationing in Shanghai was not fixed, but the army and the American community expected it to stay in Shanghai for the summer and return to the Philippines in the autumn. Therefore, this order was quite unexpected for them.

Concession Telephone Workers

Quietly Awaiting Company's Reply

Representatives of Arrested Workers Released Yesterday

Strike Committee Held Delegates' Congress Yesterday

Workers from Repair Shop and Others Join the Strike

After the workers of the Concession Telephone Company went on strike, the company delayed negotiations because the conditions had not yet been translated. Yesterday, workers from the Yangshupu Repair Shop, the Yidingpan Road Wiring Room, and the Fujian Road Sample Room also joined the strike, and the situation expanded. The Strike Committee convened a delegates' congress, and the unemployed workers who were laid off before May 30th also joined the unified action and put forward demands. The details are as follows:

Negotiations Delayed: The Strike Committee sent representatives to negotiate the conditions with the company the day before yesterday. The company said that the conditions had not yet been translated and still did not give a definite reply, causing the negotiations to stall. It is now heard that the company has completed the translation of the conditions put forward by the workers and will reply on Monday. However, the reporter from the New Voice News Agency met with worker representative Ye Gongzhao yesterday, who said that they have not yet received any notice from the company. It is now decided to strictly organize the Strike Committee and quietly await the company's reply.

Strike Expanded: After the workers of the Jiangxi Road Central Bank and the branch warehouse went on strike, some workers had not yet gone on strike because they had not received orders from the Strike Committee. Yesterday morning, more than 300 workers from the Yangshupu Repair Shop, the Yidingpan Road Wiring Room, and the Fujian Road Main Wiring Room and Sample Room sent representatives to contact the Strike Committee and declared that they were willing to go on strike together. They had only not implemented it because they had not received orders. The Strike Committee believed that the management had no intention of negotiating and immediately ordered the workers of the above lines to go on strike immediately. Therefore, yesterday morning, the strike was implemented, and representatives were sent to participate in the Strike Committee.

Arrested Released: When the striking workers held a congress in front of the new Central Bank on Fujian Road the day before yesterday, the patrolmen arrested the worker representative Ye Gongzhao and the workers Wan Ruichun, Zhang Rongsheng, and Zhu Ziwen for disturbing the peace by shouting slogans. They were completely released yesterday. When Ye Gongzhao and others left the patrol station, the workers of the new Central Bank on Fujian Road held a special welcoming meeting and unanimously decided to fight to the end. It is also heard that the five members of the struggle committee organized by the striking workers in the north line of Hainin Road who were arrested by the patrolmen at the Aiwenyi Road Tongshang Hotel the day before yesterday have been released by the patrol station.

Delegates' Congress: The internal organization of the striking workers this time is very strict. Before the strike, workers from each line elected representatives to organize the delegates' congress. Yesterday at 1:00 p.m., the fourth delegates' congress was convened at Luochun Pavilion, with more than 60 representatives attending. First, the chairman reported that the management had used the excuse that the conditions had not been translated to delay negotiations and at the same time had bought off labor spies to undermine the strike. Now the workers should unite more and fight to the end to seek final victory. When the meeting was held, the patrolmen came to ban it, but the worker representatives insisted on continuing the meeting and immediately resolved: (1) To improve the organization itself and expand the Strike Committee. The 15 members additionally elected by the Public Sports Ground workers' congress the day before yesterday will be added to the Strike Committee. Each line and department will immediately establish a picket team, a propaganda team, and a fundraising team and concentrate them, and under the leadership of the Strike Committee, consolidate the group organization. (2) To make the strike work more active and prevent the company's telegrams and telephone calls. (3) To expand propaganda to the outside world, request assistance from all walks of life, and send representatives to various places to request assistance from workers. (4) To receive newspaper reporters and publish the third declaration, which will be handed over to the Propaganda Department for execution. (5) To raise strike funds. It was decided to collect half a yuan from each worker and also raise funds from the outside world. (6) The external propaganda must be unified (decided to be handed over to the Propaganda Department for execution). (7) To publish a strike tabloid (to be handled by the Propaganda Department). (8) To participate in today's congress. (9) To establish a new office.

Meetings of Various Lines: The enlarged meeting of the Strike Committee of the Fujian Road Line was held at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, with 27 people attending. It was resolved: (1) Each striking worker should participate in the picket team, the propaganda team, the fundraising team, and other work. (2) To improve the work of each department and expand the organization of the transportation team. (3) To pass the third strike declaration. (4) To review the work of the presidium of the General Strike Committee. (5) The entire body to participate in the congress. Also, the North Line Struggle Committee held a meeting at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, with more than 20 people attending. It was resolved: (1) All striking workers should participate in the work of various organizations of the Strike Committee. (2) To improve the group. (3) The entire body to participate in the congress. (4) To start warning the female switchboard operators about their unconscious actions and invite them to participate in the Strike Committee. (5) To establish a worker reception center. (6) To make suggestions to the delegates' congress: (1) To expand the Strike Committee. (2) To improve the work of each line, department, and group. (3) The Strike Committee's finances and work should be regularly reported to the masses. Also, the workers of the air-conditioning rooms of various lines also held a meeting yesterday, with more than 20 people attending. It was resolved: (2) To donate half a yuan each to the strike fund, which was collected at the time. (2) To participate in the congress. (3) To establish an air-conditioning worker affairs committee, electing eight members. (4) To organize a propaganda team and a picket team.

Worker Negotiations: In the past year or so, the Electric Company has successively dismissed more than a thousand workers. Many unemployed workers have not yet received severance pay or have only received one or two months' salary. Now some unemployed workers have put forward the idea of asking the company to reissue severance pay, uniformly six months' salary. It is heard that the striking workers agree with this proposal. Workers and staff members with monthly salaries of more than 40 yuan have also proposed to the Strike Committee that they should all increase their salaries, regardless of Chinese or foreign workers and staff members. It is heard that the Strike Committee also agrees with this proposal. It is said that these two new conditions will also appear in the strike conditions.

Solution to the Electric Workers' Strike of the Chinese Merchants

The Union Believes That the Board of Directors' Handling Is Satisfactory

All the workers of the Chinese Merchants Electric Company opposed the dismissal of ticket seller No. 71 by Zhu Shaoyi, the section chief of the car service department, posted large slogans, and drove Zhu Shaoyi away. The situation of petitioning the manager was serious, and there was a tendency to brew a strike. Now the company's board of directors has resolved to allow the resumption of work, and the workers believe that it is satisfactory. The dark clouds have cleared away in an instant. The details are as follows:

Cause of the Dispute: Zhu Shaoyi, the section chief of the car service department of the company, dismissed ticket seller No. 71 for allegedly skimming oil. All the workers believed that Zhu Shaoyi had dismissed the worker for no reason and believed that he intended to oppress them. The First District Water and Electricity Industry Union sent personnel to negotiate, but it was ineffective, leading to a tendency to brew a strike. The day before yesterday, the union specially convened a delegates' congress to discuss measures. Because it was during martial law, the Public Security Bureau dissuaded them, so the meeting was not held. The next day, they petitioned the company, requesting the company to replace Zhu Shaoyi and allow ticket seller No. 71 to resume work. The company agreed to reply after the board of directors discussed it.

Satisfactory Solution: The Chinese Merchants Electric Company held a board of directors meeting yesterday. Regarding the dismissal of ticket seller No. 71 by Zhu Shaoyi, the section chief of the car service department, after the standing directors reviewed it, they submitted it for discussion. They all believed that Zhu Shaoyi's handling was inappropriate, and the service of ticket seller No. 71 was not without negligence. They should be given appropriate punishment separately. Ticket seller No. 71 should still be allowed to resume work, and the salary during the suspension of work should be paid as usual. The rest of the case will be continued to be investigated and handled by the board of directors. It is heard that the First District Water and Electricity Industry Union believes that the board of directors' handling is satisfactory, so the strike was eliminated without a trace.

Consulted Yesterday on the Revitalization of the City Center Area

Promote the Establishment of a Fund Management Committee

Regarding the issue of the revitalization of the city center area, Secretary-General Yu was ordered to convene the directors of the Land, Finance, Works, and Public Utilities Bureaus to a meeting at the Municipal Government at 10:30 a.m. yesterday. Cai Zengji, Director of the Finance Bureau, Jin Liren, Director of the Land Bureau, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, and Shen Yi, Director of the Works Bureau, all attended. This will not only make the project actively proceed but also make the foundation of the city center area more and more solid. The candidates for the Fund Management Committee will be elected by the landholders to show caution. It is heard that the total amount of the fund, including the first phase of the project, is about 3 million yuan. Since the January 28th Incident, although the municipal government's finances have been extremely strained, not a single penny of this fund has been used.

To Negotiate the Formation of the Aviation National Salvation Association

Huang Bingheng, Director of the Aviation Administration, believes that national defense is weak and aviation is very immature, and it seems necessary to actively expand and promote it. Issued by the United Reserve Committee

Public Bill, Treasury Bill, and Mortgage Bill

After the member banks of the Shanghai United Reserve Committee successively paid up their reserve assets, they have issued the three types of bills, namely public bills, treasury bills, and mortgage bills. These reserve assets have been accurately reviewed by experts and then strictly evaluated, so the guarantee of the bills is extremely solid. For the public bill item, the committee has raised sufficient funds for payment. In addition to the original receiving bank holding it to borrow funds from the committee, if it is issued by the bank, it can be used in the market to fully replace cash. The committee is responsible for paying the bill holder immediately upon sight of the bill and redeeming it in full at any time. This kind of circulating securities is still a new creation in the market. After it is used, not only can the funds between banks become more active, but the exquisite printing, convenient delivery, and solid credit should be welcomed by the commercial sector. As for treasury bills and mortgage bills, their circulation is limited to banks. This newspaper has specially obtained a sample of public bills and treasury bills from the committee (the design of the mortgage bill is roughly the same as that of the treasury bill) and shrunk them to the left to provide to readers.

French Fleet in China

New Commander Pierre-Alexis Ronarc'h Arrives in Shanghai

French Consulate Welcomed Yesterday

The Ta Mei Wan Pao reported that Vice Admiral Pierre-Alexis Ronarc'h, the new commander of the French fleet in China, arrived in Shanghai on the cruiser Primauguet yesterday afternoon (the 10th) and docked in the Huangpu River in front of the Jiangnan Shipyard. The French Consul General Meyrier immediately boarded the ship to pay a visit. Soon after, Ronarc'h also disembarked by boat to return the visit. Important members of the French community went to the pier to welcome him. Ronarc'h met with Consul General Meyrier and Army Commander Colonel Max for about half an hour before departing. It is now scheduled to take the original ship to Hankou on the 15th of this month and then transfer to a French gunboat to inspect the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. After that, the cruiser Primauguet will go to the Zhejiang overseas area to participate in summer exercises. This morning (the 11th), the French Consul General welcomed the new commander at the consulate.

British Candy Store as a Gift

Donation to Shanghai War Zone Children

A message from the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Child Welfare Association states that the director of the Shanghai War Zone Orphanage and Asylum recently received a letter from the owner of Cadbarg Bros. Ltd. (a confectionery shop in London, England), stating that they were deeply saddened to hear of the suffering of children in the Shanghai war zone. At the request of Lady Merield Paget, president of the British Save the Children Fund, the shop has decided to donate cocoa and chocolate candies worth 50 British pounds (equivalent to 800 Chinese yuan), to be shipped to China on May 6th aboard the SS格兰盖里. These items will be distributed by the Shanghai War Zone Orphanage and Asylum, as well as other relevant organizations. The compassion of these foreign friends in providing relief to children is truly commendable. It is noted that the Shanghai War Zone Orphanage and Asylum is jointly established by the Chinese Child Welfare Association, the Shanghai Citizens' Local Maintenance Association, and the British Save the Children Fund. It has sheltered a total of 95 child refugees. To date, 37 of them have been taken in by others, including 13 by their parents, 4 by relatives, 4 by teachers, 5 adopted as godchildren, 1 apprenticed, and 10 placed in other child welfare organizations. The director of the asylum is Miss Christopher Chancellcr, wife of Mr. Zhang Xuelou, president of Reuters, and daughter of Lady Murield Paget, president of the British Save the Children Fund.

Zhenjiang Fellow-Provincials Association

Request for the Abolition of the Pacification Commissioner's Office

The Zhenjiang Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai sends an urgent telegram to Wang, President of the Executive Yuan of the National Government, and Chiang, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, stating: "It is reported that the Jiangsu Provincial Pacification Commissioner's Office has been effectively closed. Upon hearing this news, the public is in a state of anxiety. We have found that in various counties of Jiangsu Province, especially in the areas of Jiangbei, Yangtong, and Huaihai, bandits are rampant, and the people cannot sleep peacefully. Fortunately, since the establishment of the Pacification Commissioner's Office, with Pacification Commissioner Zhang in charge, bandits have gone into hiding, and the region has been able to maintain peace and order. If it is hastily abolished, we fear that the situation will reignite, and villains will seek to act recklessly. In addition, last year's floods in the province, coupled with the failure of this year's spring harvest, have resulted in a large number of refugees and a proliferation of bandits, posing hidden dangers that cause the people to feel as if a great calamity is about to befall them. Therefore, we dare to convey the people's sentiments by sending this telegram to you, humbly requesting that you take the local situation into consideration, heed the public's opinion, and temporarily postpone the abolition of the Pacification Commissioner's Office to maintain order. Depending on the abundance of this year's autumn harvest, the local situation can be assessed, and appropriate measures can be taken accordingly. This would be a blessing for the region, a benefit for the people, and also a contribution to the Party and the nation. We are sending this urgent telegram with the utmost urgency and awaiting your instructions. Respectfully, Xu Qiufan, Wu Yunzhai, Bu Shaoru, and others from the Zhenjiang Five-County Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai."

Pudong Fellow-Provincials Association

Request to Cancel the Ministry's Approval of Increased Grain Tax

The collection will continue according to the original plan for the 20th year.

Exemption from collection will be implemented from the 21st year onwards.

On March 2nd, the Ministry of Finance responded to the Pudong Fellow-Provincials Association's request to cancel the additional levy of two yuan on grain tax imposed in the winter of the 20th year: "We have received your petition. Upon review, the petition states that Jiangsu Province requested the additional levy in April of last year, at a time when the signs of disaster were not yet apparent and reports of successive floods had not yet been received, which is indeed the case. Regarding the request to cancel the additional levy of two yuan, we request further instructions from the Executive Yuan after a factual report." This is the reply.

Furthermore, on June 10th, the association received an urgent telegram from the Ministry of Finance: "To the Shanghai Pudong Fellow-Provincials Association: Regarding the case of the additional levy of two yuan on grain tax in Jiangsu in the winter of the 20th year, we previously reported the matter to the Executive Yuan for review and instructions after receiving your association's request for cancellation. Subsequently, we received an order from the Executive Yuan approving the Jiangsu Provincial Government's request to report to the Department of Finance, proposing that the matter be left as it is and requesting a review of the original report, as the points mentioned in the Department's original report were factual. The reasons put forward by the council members in their original report were: first, the original plan was limited to one time in the 19th year, and the extension to the 20th year was a pretext, and it is feared that similar requests will be made in the future, which would be a breach of national trust; second, Jiangsu Province's regulations stipulate that the land tax in each county shall not exceed 1% of the land price, and this additional levy exceeds the 1% range; third, last year was a year of great famine, and taxes should be reduced to alleviate the people's suffering, which is also well-founded. Now that the 20th year is coming to an end, the extension of the additional levy is about to expire. In accordance with the Executive Yuan's approval of the original plan, the extension cannot be renewed under any pretext after the expiration. In order to take into account both the provincial treasury and the people's difficulties, it is suggested that the additional levy on grain tax in Jiangsu for the 20th year should be allowed to continue to be collected according to the original plan, and the Executive Yuan should reiterate its previous order that the deadline for the additional levy on grain tax in Jiangsu should never be extended, and that the exemption should be implemented from the 21st year onwards, in order to show great trust and alleviate the people's difficulties. The Executive Yuan has reviewed and approved the report and ordered compliance. We are now ordered by the Executive Yuan that this case should be directly discussed and handled by the Ministry in consultation with the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and a report should be submitted for review and decision. This is the order. Ministry of Finance (Seal)."

Director of the Navigation Administration Bureau

He Hanlan Assumed Office Yesterday

Xi Dingmo, Director of the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau, was transferred to Tianjin by order of the Ministry, and He Hanlan succeeded him. At 9:00 AM yesterday, the new director arrived in Shanghai to take office, and the handover was as follows:

Inauguration Speech: At 9:00 AM yesterday, the new director, He Hanlan, accompanied by Xia Sunpeng and others, arrived at the Navigation Administration Bureau at No. 6 Sichuan Road, where he was greeted by the former director, Xi Dingmo. After a brief rest, they went to the auditorium to hold the inauguration ceremony. The order was very simple. All the bureau staff and the director of the Ningbo Branch were present. Important figures in the Shanghai navigation industry also came to the bureau to attend the ceremony. After the handover ceremony, He Hanlan delivered an inauguration speech, stating that the navigation administration is related to the nation's transportation lifeline and is also linked to commerce. He said that China's navigation industry is still in its infancy, which is undeniable, but it is due to the end of unequal treaties that a situation of guests becoming masters has been created. He said that he was ordered to come to the bureau to study how to revitalize navigation affairs and strive to achieve the hope of fully recovering navigation rights. He said that the former director had achieved great success in handling navigation administration, and that he would follow his example, and so on.

Page 16

Appointment of Staff: The bureau's organization is divided into two sections:

Divided into Documentation Section, General Affairs Section, Statistics Section, Audit Section, Accounting Section, Ship Inspection Section, Registration Section, Certificate Issuance Section, etc. The duties of the first section are internal affairs of the bureau, while the second section is responsible for technology and navigation administration. Yao Zi, the original director of the first section, had already resigned. Sheng Pinru, the director of the second section, also resigned. Director He then appointed Xu Shiruo as the director of the first section and Wu Daming as the director of the second section, concurrently serving as the chief of technology. Zhang Shucheng was appointed as the chief of the accounting section. Some of the other section chiefs and clerks have also been reassigned.

Committee Members Supervise Inventory: The Ministry of Transportation specially appointed Xia Sunpeng as a committee member to supervise the inventory. Yesterday, after former Director Xi handed over the official documents and files, Xia Sunpeng supervised the new staff in receiving and verifying the items. The process was completed at 11:00 AM, and there were no errors. Xia then sent a telegram to the Ministry, reporting that the inventory was accurate. After the new director took over the seal of office, former Director Xi left at around 12:00 PM. According to Xi, he plans to rest for a few days before setting a date to go to Tianjin.

Brief Biography of the Director: The new director, He Hanlan, whose courtesy name is Xuehai, is a native of Guangdong. He is a graduate of the Huangpu Naval Academy in Guangdong and the Nanjing Naval Officers' School. He has served as the Chief of Staff of the Naval Headquarters, Captain of the Feimo Warship, Chief of the Construction Supervision Section of the Jiangnan Shipyard, and Director of the Qingdao Police Department. He has also served as a captain in the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Wu Daming, the director of the second section, is a graduate of the Haidong School in Guangdong. He has served as the Director of the Ship Inspection Office of the Ministry of Finance, the Director of the Yangtze River Patrol Bureau, and the General Supervisor of the Jiangnan Shipyard.

Gan Jiehou Has No Intention of Leaving Shanghai

Gan Jiehou, the former Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, returned to Shanghai not long after resigning and married Ms. Xu Wanjun. He is currently on his honeymoon. According to Gan, recent reports in the newspapers stating that he had plans to go south were inaccurate and that he has no intention of leaving Shanghai.

Continued Report on the Newspaper Labor Strike

The arrested workers have all been released.

The Newspaper Workers' Union went on strike on the 1st of this month, involving the Shen Bao, Xin Shen Bao, and Shi Bao, in a united action due to the dismissal of workers by the Shi Shi Xin Bao. Subsequently, Mr. Du Yuesheng mediated and the strike was called off. On the 8th, the Criminal Investigation Team of the Public Security Bureau arrested more than 20 former Shi Shi Xin Bao workers who were staying at the Newspaper Workers' Union. Thanks to the rescue efforts of various parties, they were all released yesterday.

A spokesperson for the Newspaper Workers' Union stated that since the arrest of more than 20 former Shi Shi Xin Bao workers staying at the union on the 8th of this month, instigated by the management of the Shi Shi Xin Bao, the union issued a declaration the day before yesterday, requesting that all sectors uphold justice. This was followed yesterday by the "Sincere Announcement to Society" published by the Shi Shi Xin Bao and the letter from Mr. Zha Renwei, representing the newspaper, to the Shen Bao and Xin Shen Bao, making corrections. On the surface, the so-called justice, national law, human sentiment, and responsibility are all grand and eloquent, but an analysis of the causes and consequences of this labor dispute will clearly show where the responsibility lies. This labor dispute was entirely caused by the Shi Shi Xin Bao's management's desire to destroy the union's organization, stemming from a failed attempt to print the Da Wan Bao on commission. Initially, all the workers were forced to leave the workplace, and then advertisements were placed in the newspapers to recruit former workers (the workers who returned to work were required to fill out a volunteer form, absolutely obey the newspaper's regulations, and leave the union). This was intended to break up the solidarity of all the workers, and the intentions were obvious to everyone. Subsequently, despite several attempts at mediation by the union and well-meaning parties from the outside, and despite the former workers going to the residence of Mr. Zhang Zhuping, the chairman of the board of directors of the newspaper, several times to petition to return to work, the management of the newspaper remained unmoved. Therefore, the union's entire membership went on strike on the 1st of this month to urge the newspaper's management to reflect. Mr. Du Yuesheng then mediated, and the Shen Bao, Xin Shen Bao, and Shi Bao first resumed work. The dismissal of workers by the Shi Shi Xin Bao was to be resolved by Mr. Du after consulting with the management of the Shi Shi Xin Bao. Unexpectedly, during the period of negotiations between the two parties, the Criminal Investigation Team of the Public Security Bureau came to the union on the 8th of this month and arrested the Shi Shi Xin Bao workers who had been forced to leave. This was not only unfortunate for the arrested workers of the union, but also unexpected by the mediator. The management of the newspaper had already forced these workers into unemployment and was still not satisfied, but wanted to imprison them. How can this be reconciled with the so-called justice, national law, human sentiment, and responsibility? Furthermore, in the correction letter sent by the Shi Shi Xin Bao's representative lawyer, Zha Renwei, to the Shen Bao and Xin Shen Bao yesterday, it was stated that the union's equipment and belongings were not destroyed. This is a matter of fact, and the union would not dare to falsely accuse anyone. We are currently investigating the destroyed equipment and belongings and taking photographs, which will soon be made public to society. In short, the union's destruction is not only a humiliation for the union, but also a disgrace for all the workers in Shanghai. Although the union is in this unfavorable environment, it does not avoid hardship or fear, and is resolutely fighting for the sake of opening up a glimmer of hope for the dim labor movement in Shanghai. Although the subjective views of labor and management are different, the truth, fairness, and justice will have their own public opinion.

China National Aviation Corporation

The Shanghai-Chengdu Route is Renamed the Shanghai-Sichuan Route

The China National Aviation Corporation's route from Shanghai to Chengdu was previously named the Shanghai-Chengdu Route because Chengdu's ancient name was Furong (Hibiscus) City. However, the public did not find the use of the character "Rong" to represent Chengdu very clear and often had doubts. Moreover, the route currently only goes to Chongqing, so it would be more appropriate to use the character "Shu" (Sichuan). Therefore, the General Manager, Liu Peiquan, has changed the name of the route to the Shanghai-Sichuan Route in the hope of making it easier to understand, and has reported it to the Ministry of Transportation for record.

The Native Cloth Exhibition Starts on the 13th

Public Exhibition at Penglai Market

The Shanghai County Farmers' Education Center, in order to promote the idea of ​​Chinese people using native cloth and to increase farmers' production, specifically initiated the holding of a county-wide native cloth exhibition. It opened on the 6th of this month at the Zhuanqiao Farmers' Lecture Hall, and is touring the various districts of the county every day. Everywhere it goes, the public enthusiastically participates, which is beneficial to promoting the future of domestic products. From the 13th to the 15th of this month, it will be exhibited in Shanghai for three days. It was originally scheduled to be held at the county government, but the center is concerned that the venue will be too crowded to accommodate everyone who wishes to attend, so it has been changed to the Penglai Market. Yesterday, the center specially invited all sectors of Shanghai to visit and provide guidance. The original letter is copied below: "To whom it may concern: Our center is holding a native cloth exhibition from June 6th in order to make the Chinese people understand the advantages of native cloth, arouse their awareness of using native cloth, promote agricultural products, improve their lives, and provide farmers with opportunities to compete. It will be publicly exhibited at Penglai Market in your city from June 13th to 15th. The closing ceremony will be held at 10:00 am on the 15th. After the closing ceremony, we will also organize a native cloth improvement association, a native cloth showroom, and a native cloth store. We respectfully ask you to visit and provide guidance, so that we may have a standard to follow. We are deeply eager."

New Facilities at the Ningbo Industrial Bank

Since the official opening of the Ningbo Industrial Bank in this city on the 4th, the business has been very prosperous. All the staff of the bank uphold the purpose of serving society, treat customers courteously, and strive for efficiency in all procedures. Now, in order to facilitate all sectors, the business hours have been extended. All types of deposits on Sundays will be open as usual in the morning and afternoon, and the interest rates offered are also more favorable.
